# FEV1 in childhood asthma (Wu 2014)

## Model and source

- Citation: Wu K, Gamazon ER, Im HK, Geeleher P, White SR, Solway J,
  Clemmer GL, Weiss ST, Tantisira KG, Cox NJ, Ratain MJ, Huang RS.
  Genome-wide interrogation of longitudinal FEV1 in children with
  asthma. Am J Respir Crit Care Med 2014;190(6):619-627.
  <doi:10.1164/rccm.201403-0460OC>.
- Description: Longitudinal nonlinear mixed-effects disease-progression
  model of pre-bronchodilator forced expiratory volume in 1 second
  (FEV1) in children with asthma, fit to 1,041 participants in the
  Childhood Asthma Management Program (CAMP) study (Wu 2014). The
  structural model is an exponential function of age and height with a
  race-stratified intercept and an additive treatment-arm effect for
  inhaled budesonide on the linear-scale FEV1; nedocromil shows no
  significant effect and is pooled into the placebo reference. The model
  has no PK component – the inhaled-corticosteroid effect is encoded as
  a per-subject binary treatment-arm indicator (CONMED_BUDESONIDE).
- Article: <https://doi.org/10.1164/rccm.201403-0460OC>

## Population

Wu 2014 developed the longitudinal FEV1 model from the n = 1,041
children with mild to moderate persistent asthma enrolled in the
Childhood Asthma Management Program (CAMP) randomized controlled trial
(NEJM 2000;343:1054-1063). The trial used three arms with stratified
randomization: placebo (n = 418), inhaled nedocromil 8 mg twice daily (n
= 312), and inhaled budesonide 200 microg twice daily (n = 311). FEV1
was measured every 2-4 months before bronchodilator administration over
up to 4 years of follow-up. Mean (SD) age at enrolment was ~9 (2) years;
~40% of subjects were female; the self-reported race distribution was
68.4% White, 13.3% Black / African American, 9.4% Mexican American, and
8.9% Other (computed by pooling the per-arm counts from Table 1 of Wu
2014). The trial was conducted at eight clinical sites in the United
States.

The same information is available programmatically via
`readModelDb("Wu_2014_FEV1_asthma")$population` after the model is
loaded.

## Source trace

The structural model is paper Equation 3 with an additive treatment-arm
term on linear-scale FEV1:

``` math
\mathrm{FEV1}(t) \;=\; \exp(\theta_{\mathrm{age}} \cdot \mathrm{AGE} \;+\; \theta_{\mathrm{ht}} \cdot \mathrm{HT} \;-\; \theta_{\mathrm{int}}) \;+\; \theta_{\mathrm{drug}} \cdot \mathbb{1}\{\mathrm{arm} = \mathrm{budesonide}\}
```

The race-stratified intercept (paper Table 2 reports three values: 1.89
for White / Mexican American, 2.04 for African American, 1.95 for Other)
is re-parameterised in the model file as one reference intercept
(`theta_int = 1.89`, White / Mexican American as reference) plus two
additive race deltas (`e_race_black_int = 0.15`,
`e_race_other_int = 0.06`). This is an exact algebraic
reparameterisation – summing reference + delta returns the paper’s three
published values.

| Equation / parameter | Value | Source location |
|----|---:|----|
| `theta_age` (rate of change with AGE) | 0.0137 1/year | Table 2 NONMEM final (theta1; RSE 16.1%) |
| `theta_ht` (rate of change with HT) | 0.0169 1/cm | Table 2 NONMEM final (theta2; RSE 2.20%) |
| `theta_int` (reference intercept, White / Mexican American) | 1.89 | Table 2 NONMEM final (theta3 White/Mexican; RSE 1.78%) |
| `e_race_black_int` (additive delta for RACE_BLACK = 1) | 0.15 | Table 2: 2.04 (African American) - 1.89 (White/Mexican); paper Results “the FEV1 level … was significantly lower in African American children with asthma” |
| `e_race_other_int` (additive delta for RACE_OTHER = 1) | 0.06 | Table 2: 1.95 (Others) - 1.89 (White/Mexican) |
| `e_conmed_budesonide_fev1` (additive budesonide effect on FEV1) | 0.103 L | Table 2 NONMEM final (theta_drugeffect; RSE 14.1%); paper Results “FEV1 with long-term treatment of budesonide was predicted to be 0.103 +/- 0.129 higher” |
| IIV SD on `theta_age` (`etatheta_age`) | 0.00722 | Table 2 NONMEM final (shrinkage 32.9%); variance 5.21e-5 |
| IIV SD on `theta_int` (`etatheta_int`) | 0.0912 | Table 2 NONMEM final (shrinkage 26.4%); variance 8.32e-3 |
| IIV SD on `e_conmed_budesonide_fev1` | 0.129 L | Table 2 NONMEM final (shrinkage 67.3%); variance 1.66e-2 |
| IIV on `theta_ht` (theta2) | fixed to 0 | Paper Results: “theta2’s interindividual variability was very small (less than 10^-6) … fixed to zero” |
| Proportional residual CV | 5.91% | Table 2 NONMEM final intraindividual variability proportional (shrinkage 4.52%) |
| Additive residual SD | 0.0863 L | Table 2 NONMEM final intraindividual variability additive (shrinkage 4.52%) |
| Exponential structural model selected over linear | n/a | Methods: “The best prediction for FEV1 was achieved by an exponential function of age and height”; Table E1 (supplementary) reports the AIC comparison favouring the exponential form |
| Race retained as the only categorical covariate | n/a | Results: “only race was found to be a key covariate”; sex, BMI, body weight rejected by Delta-OFV \< 3.84 |
| Nedocromil pooled into the placebo reference | n/a | Results: “Nedocromil did not show any significant effect on FEV1 when compared with the placebo group” |

## Errata

No published erratum or corrigendum was found for this paper as of the
model extraction date (2026-06-12).

One notational caveat is worth flagging for readers: paper Table 1
reports a mean (SD) “Height” of 55.3 (28.8) cm, 56.0 (28.7) cm, and 56.8
(28.0) cm across the placebo / nedocromil / budesonide arms. These
values are implausibly low for 9-year-old children (typical standing
height ~125 to 135 cm at age 9 per WHO 2007 references) and the SD is
too large to be a unit-conversion artefact alone – the values appear to
be either centred deviations or a column-labelling error in the
published Table 1. The structural model itself uses HT in cm at the
per-observation level and the fitted `theta_ht = 0.0169 1/cm` is
consistent with the published model predictions in Figures 1 and 2, so
this vignette assumes the model is to be applied with absolute standing
height in cm (the convention assumed in paediatric spirometry references
such as Hankinson 1999) and treats Table 1’s “Height” entries as a
transcription anomaly, not as the units the model consumes.

## Virtual cohort

Original individual-level FEV1 data from CAMP are not directly
redistributable without dbGaP access (the paper uses dbGaP accession
phs000424.v3.p1.c1). The simulations below use a virtual cohort whose
covariate distributions approximate Table 1 of Wu 2014: ages drawn
approximately uniformly across the 5-13 year observed range, height
drawn from a normal distribution centred on a WHO-typical mid-cohort
value (130 cm at age 9; SD = 12 cm to reflect the within-age variation
across the 5-13 year span actually present in CAMP), race indicators
drawn from a multinomial distribution matching the pooled Table 1 race
fractions (68.4% White, 13.3% African American, 9.4% Mexican American,
8.9% Other), and treatment-arm indicator drawn from a multinomial
matching the trial randomisation fractions (40.2% placebo, 30.0%
nedocromil, 29.9% budesonide). The placebo and nedocromil arms are
pooled into the reference (`CONMED_BUDESONIDE = 0`).

``` r

set.seed(20260612)

n_subj <- 200L   # virtual subjects for the covariate-distribution summary + height-for-age smoother

cohort <- tibble::tibble(
  id  = seq_len(n_subj),
  AGE = runif(n_subj, min = 5, max = 13),       # years (CAMP enrolment + follow-up span)
  HT  = pmax(80, rnorm(n_subj, mean = 130, sd = 12))  # cm (absolute standing height; clamped low to keep physically plausible)
)

# Race assignment matching pooled Table 1 fractions: pool White and Mexican
# American into the reference group (theta_int = 1.89), per the published
# parameterisation. RACE_BLACK and RACE_OTHER are the modelled indicators.
race_group <- sample(
  c("WhiteMex", "Black", "Other"),
  size    = n_subj,
  replace = TRUE,
  prob    = c(0.778, 0.133, 0.089)              # 0.684 + 0.094 = 0.778 (pooled White/Mexican); 0.133 Black; 0.089 Other
)
cohort$RACE_BLACK <- as.integer(race_group == "Black")
cohort$RACE_OTHER <- as.integer(race_group == "Other")

# Treatment-arm assignment matching trial randomisation. Pool placebo and
# nedocromil into the reference (CONMED_BUDESONIDE = 0) per the paper's
# finding of no significant nedocromil effect.
arm <- sample(
  c("placebo", "nedocromil", "budesonide"),
  size    = n_subj,
  replace = TRUE,
  prob    = c(418, 312, 311) / 1041
)
cohort$CONMED_BUDESONIDE <- as.integer(arm == "budesonide")
cohort$arm <- arm

cat(sprintf(
  "Cohort: n = %d; AGE range = %.1f to %.1f y; HT range = %.0f to %.0f cm\n",
  n_subj, min(cohort$AGE), max(cohort$AGE), min(cohort$HT), max(cohort$HT)
))
#> Cohort: n = 200; AGE range = 5.0 to 13.0 y; HT range = 105 to 160 cm
cat(sprintf(
  "Race: WhiteMex = %d (%.1f%%); Black = %d (%.1f%%); Other = %d (%.1f%%)\n",
  sum(race_group == "WhiteMex"), 100 * mean(race_group == "WhiteMex"),
  sum(race_group == "Black"),    100 * mean(race_group == "Black"),
  sum(race_group == "Other"),    100 * mean(race_group == "Other")
))
#> Race: WhiteMex = 152 (76.0%); Black = 29 (14.5%); Other = 19 (9.5%)
cat(sprintf(
  "Arms: placebo = %d; nedocromil = %d; budesonide = %d\n",
  sum(arm == "placebo"), sum(arm == "nedocromil"), sum(arm == "budesonide")
))
#> Arms: placebo = 80; nedocromil = 54; budesonide = 66
```

## Simulation

The model has no PK dose events. The dataset’s `time` column carries
each subject’s age in years directly; the observation `fev1` is
evaluated at the supplied age. Build a one-observation-per-subject event
table at each subject’s covariate point (the simulations below are
interested in the typical-value FEV1 at the subject’s own age) and a
separate per-subject age-sweep table for the longitudinal trajectory.

``` r

mod <- readModelDb("Wu_2014_FEV1_asthma")

# Per-subject typical-value FEV1 at the assigned (AGE, HT, race, arm).
events_per_subj <- cohort |>
  dplyr::transmute(
    id, time = AGE, evid = 0L, amt = 0,
    HT, RACE_BLACK, RACE_OTHER, CONMED_BUDESONIDE
  )

sim_per_subj <- rxode2::rxSolve(
  rxode2::zeroRe(mod),                          # typical-value (no IIV) per subject
  events = events_per_subj,
  keep   = c("HT", "RACE_BLACK", "RACE_OTHER", "CONMED_BUDESONIDE")
) |>
  as.data.frame() |>
  dplyr::left_join(cohort |> dplyr::select(id, arm), by = "id")
#> ℹ parameter labels from comments will be replaced by 'label()'
#> ℹ omega/sigma items treated as zero: 'etatheta_age', 'etatheta_int', 'etae_conmed_budesonide_fev1'
#> Warning: multi-subject simulation without without 'omega'
```

## Replicate published figures

### Figure 2-like: typical-value FEV1 trajectory by treatment arm

Paper Figure 2 shows a visual predictive check of the final model:
observed FEV1 against age, with the median and 5th / 95th
prediction-interval lines superimposed, split into two panels – (A)
placebo + nedocromil pooled and (B) budesonide. The paper-reported
behaviour is a steady rise of FEV1 with age, with the budesonide arm
sitting ~0.10 L above the placebo arm at every age. We reproduce the
typical-value backbone of that VPC (the deterministic expectation across
the median height-for-age curve of the cohort) below.

``` r

# Build a smooth age sweep at the cohort-median height for each arm. The
# paper's Figure 2 is a function of age alone (height co-varies with age in
# children), so we approximate the median-height-for-age relationship by
# linearly interpolating cohort height over the 5 to 13 year range.
ht_smoother <- with(cohort, approxfun(AGE, HT, ties = list("ordered", mean)))

age_grid <- seq(5, 13, by = 0.1)
trajectory <- tidyr::expand_grid(
  AGE = age_grid,
  arm = c("placebo+nedocromil", "budesonide")
) |>
  dplyr::mutate(
    id                = dplyr::row_number(),
    HT                = ht_smoother(AGE),
    RACE_BLACK        = 0L,
    RACE_OTHER        = 0L,
    CONMED_BUDESONIDE = as.integer(arm == "budesonide")
  )

events_traj <- trajectory |>
  dplyr::transmute(id, time = AGE, evid = 0L, amt = 0,
                   HT, RACE_BLACK, RACE_OTHER, CONMED_BUDESONIDE)

sim_traj <- rxode2::rxSolve(
  rxode2::zeroRe(mod),
  events = events_traj,
  keep   = c("HT", "RACE_BLACK", "RACE_OTHER", "CONMED_BUDESONIDE")
) |>
  as.data.frame() |>
  dplyr::left_join(trajectory |> dplyr::select(id, arm), by = "id")
#> ℹ parameter labels from comments will be replaced by 'label()'
#> ℹ omega/sigma items treated as zero: 'etatheta_age', 'etatheta_int', 'etae_conmed_budesonide_fev1'
#> Warning: multi-subject simulation without without 'omega'
#> Warning: column 'HT' has only 'NA' values for id '1'

    x = "Age (years)",
    y = "FEV1 (L), typical value",
    colour = "Treatment arm",
    title  = "Typical-value FEV1 vs age",
```

![Typical-value FEV1 vs age for the budesonide arm and the pooled
placebo + nedocromil arm (median-height-for-age

Typical-value FEV1 vs age for the budesonide arm and the pooled
placebo + nedocromil arm (median-height-for-age curve).

### Figure 2-like with IIV: percentile envelope by treatment arm

The same simulation with the published between-subject variability
turned back on gives a percentile envelope analogous to the VPC. The
simulation below draws subject-level etas at each age grid point
separately (so the envelope at each age is a marginal distribution over
IIV draws, matching the cohort-aggregate interpretation of Figure 2).

``` r

n_draws <- 100L   # IIV draws per age grid point per arm (VPC envelope)

events_vpc <- tidyr::expand_grid(
  draw = seq_len(n_draws),
  AGE  = age_grid,
  arm  = c("placebo+nedocromil", "budesonide")
) |>
  dplyr::mutate(
    id                = dplyr::row_number(),
    HT                = ht_smoother(AGE),
    RACE_BLACK        = 0L,
    RACE_OTHER        = 0L,
    CONMED_BUDESONIDE = as.integer(arm == "budesonide")
  )

events_vpc_et <- events_vpc |>
  dplyr::transmute(id, time = AGE, evid = 0L, amt = 0,
                   HT, RACE_BLACK, RACE_OTHER, CONMED_BUDESONIDE)

sim_vpc <- rxode2::rxSolve(
  mod,                                          # with IIV
  events = events_vpc_et,
  keep   = c("HT", "RACE_BLACK", "RACE_OTHER", "CONMED_BUDESONIDE")
) |>
  as.data.frame() |>
  dplyr::left_join(events_vpc |> dplyr::select(id, arm, draw), by = "id")
#> ℹ parameter labels from comments will be replaced by 'label()'
#> Warning: column 'HT' has only 'NA' values for id '1'
#> Warning: column 'HT' has only 'NA' values for id '2'
#> Warning: column 'HT' has only 'NA' values for id '3'
#> Warning: column 'HT' has only 'NA' values for id '4'
#> Warning: column 'HT' has only 'NA' values for id '5'
#> Warning: column 'HT' has only 'NA' values for id '6'
#> Warning: column 'HT' has only 'NA' values for id '7'
#> Warning: column 'HT' has only 'NA' values for id '8'
#> Warning: column 'HT' has only 'NA' values for id '9'
#> Warning: column 'HT' has only 'NA' values for id '10'
#> Warning: column 'HT' has only 'NA' values for id '11'
#> Warning: column 'HT' has only 'NA' values for id '12'
#> Warning: column 'HT' has only 'NA' values for id '13'
#> Warning: column 'HT' has only 'NA' values for id '14'
#> Warning: column 'HT' has only 'NA' values for id '15'

envelope <- sim_vpc |>
  dplyr::group_by(arm, time) |>
  dplyr::summarise(
    Q05 = stats::quantile(fev1, 0.05, na.rm = TRUE),
    Q50 = stats::quantile(fev1, 0.50, na.rm = TRUE),
    Q95 = stats::quantile(fev1, 0.95, na.rm = TRUE),
    .groups = "drop"
  )

ggplot(envelope, aes(x = time, fill = arm, colour = arm)) +
  geom_ribbon(aes(ymin = Q05, ymax = Q95), alpha = 0.20, linewidth = 0) +
  geom_line(aes(y = Q50), linewidth = 0.9) +
  scale_colour_manual(values = c("placebo+nedocromil" = "steelblue",
                                 "budesonide"         = "darkorange")) +
  scale_fill_manual(values   = c("placebo+nedocromil" = "steelblue",
                                 "budesonide"         = "darkorange")) +
  labs(
    x       = "Age (years)",
    y       = "FEV1 (L)",
    colour  = "Treatment arm",
    fill    = "Treatment arm",
    title   = "FEV1 median + 5th / 95th percentile envelope vs age",
    caption = "Median trajectory + 5th / 95th percentile envelope from n = 100 IIV draws per age and arm."
  ) +
  theme_bw()
```

![Typical-value FEV1 median and 5th / 95th percentile envelope vs age,
by treatment arm. Replicates the VPC envelope of Figure 2 of Wu 2014 to
first order.](Wu_2014_FEV1_asthma_files/figure-html/figure-2-vpc-1.png)

Typical-value FEV1 median and 5th / 95th percentile envelope vs age, by
treatment arm. Replicates the VPC envelope of Figure 2 of Wu 2014 to
first order.

## Analytic spot-check against the published equation

This model is a closed-form algebraic prediction (no ODE, no dosing); a
direct numerical comparison against the published Equation 3 with the
Table 2 parameter values is the strongest validation we can run. At a
9-year-old White / Mexican American non-budesonide subject with height
130 cm:

``` math
\mathrm{FEV1} \;=\; \exp(0.0137 \times 9 + 0.0169 \times 130 - 1.89) \;=\; \exp(0.4427) \;=\; 1.557~\mathrm{L}.
```

At the same subject but in the budesonide arm:

``` math
\mathrm{FEV1} \;=\; 1.557 \;+\; 0.103 \;=\; 1.660~\mathrm{L}.
```

``` r

spot <- tibble::tibble(
  AGE               = c(9, 9, 9, 9),
  HT                = c(130, 130, 130, 130),
  RACE_BLACK        = c(0L, 0L, 1L, 0L),
  RACE_OTHER        = c(0L, 0L, 0L, 0L),
  CONMED_BUDESONIDE = c(0L, 1L, 0L, 0L),
  arm_label         = c("ref",                      # White/Mex, non-bud
                        "ref + budesonide",
                        "African American, non-bud",
                        "ref, non-bud (repeat)")
)
spot$id <- seq_len(nrow(spot))

events_spot <- spot |>
  dplyr::transmute(id, time = AGE, evid = 0L, amt = 0,
                   HT, RACE_BLACK, RACE_OTHER, CONMED_BUDESONIDE)

sim_spot <- rxode2::rxSolve(
  rxode2::zeroRe(mod),
  events = events_spot
) |>
  as.data.frame()
#> ℹ parameter labels from comments will be replaced by 'label()'
#> ℹ omega/sigma items treated as zero: 'etatheta_age', 'etatheta_int', 'etae_conmed_budesonide_fev1'
#> Warning: multi-subject simulation without without 'omega'

expected <- tibble::tibble(
  arm_label = spot$arm_label,
  expected_L = c(
    exp(0.0137 * 9 + 0.0169 * 130 - 1.89),               # White/Mex ref
    exp(0.0137 * 9 + 0.0169 * 130 - 1.89) + 0.103,       # ref + budesonide additive
    exp(0.0137 * 9 + 0.0169 * 130 - (1.89 + 0.15)),      # African American
    exp(0.0137 * 9 + 0.0169 * 130 - 1.89)                # repeat
  )
)

knitr::kable(
  tibble::tibble(
    case       = spot$arm_label,
    AGE        = spot$AGE,
    HT_cm      = spot$HT,
    expected_L = expected$expected_L,
    actual_L   = sim_spot$fev1[match(spot$id, sim_spot$id)]
  ),
  digits  = 4,
  caption = "Typical-value FEV1 at age 9 with HT = 130 cm: analytic Eq. 3 vs nlmixr2lib model."
)
```

| case                      | AGE | HT_cm | expected_L | actual_L |
|:--------------------------|----:|------:|-----------:|---------:|
| ref                       |   9 |   130 |     1.5377 |   1.5377 |
| ref + budesonide          |   9 |   130 |     1.6407 |   1.6407 |
| African American, non-bud |   9 |   130 |     1.3235 |   1.3235 |
| ref, non-bud (repeat)     |   9 |   130 |     1.5377 |   1.5377 |

Typical-value FEV1 at age 9 with HT = 130 cm: analytic Eq. 3 vs
nlmixr2lib model. {.table}

The analytic and simulated values agree to numerical precision,
confirming the model file reproduces paper Equation 3 with the Table 2
parameter values exactly.

## Assumptions and deviations

- **Race-stratified intercept reparameterisation.** The paper estimates
  three independent thetas for the race-stratified intercept (Table 2:
  1.89 for White / Mexican American, 2.04 for African American, 1.95 for
  Other). The model file re-parameterises this as one reference
  intercept (`theta_int = 1.89`, White / Mexican American reference)
  plus two additive race deltas (`e_race_black_int = 0.15`,
  `e_race_other_int = 0.06`). This is an exact algebraic
  reparameterisation: at any subject’s (RACE_BLACK, RACE_OTHER)
  covariate setting, summing the reference intercept plus the
  indicator-weighted deltas reproduces the paper’s three published
  intercept values. The deltas inherit no separate IIV (the IIV is on
  `theta_int` itself).
- **Nedocromil pooled into the placebo reference.** The paper found no
  significant FEV1 effect for nedocromil and pooled it with placebo for
  the treatment-arm covariate. The model file follows that pooling:
  `CONMED_BUDESONIDE = 0` covers both placebo and nedocromil arms; the
  estimated treatment effect (`e_conmed_budesonide_fev1 = 0.103 L`)
  applies only to budesonide-arm subjects.
- **`theta_ht` IIV fixed to 0.** The paper reports the inter-individual
  variability of theta2 (rate of change with height) as “very small
  (less than 10^-6)” and fixed it to zero in the final model. The model
  file does not declare an `etatheta_ht`; only the three estimated IIVs
  (on `theta_age`, `theta_int`, `e_conmed_budesonide_fev1`) appear in
  `ini()`.
- **Table 1 height values treated as a transcription anomaly.** Paper
  Table 1 reports mean (SD) height values around 55-57 (~28) cm across
  the three arms, which are implausibly low for 9-year-old children
  (~125 to 135 cm at age 9 per WHO 2007 references). The structural
  model itself uses HT in cm at the per-observation level and the fitted
  `theta_ht = 0.0169 1/cm` is consistent with the published Figures 1
  and 2, so the model file (and this vignette) assume absolute standing
  height in cm. Treat Table 1’s “Height” column as a probable
  baseline-deviation or unit-label anomaly, not as the units the model
  consumes.
- **CAMP individual-level data not redistributable.** Direct VPC
  overlays against the paper’s Figure 2 cannot be reproduced here
  because CAMP’s per-subject FEV1 measurements are gated behind dbGaP
  accession phs000424.v3.p1.c1. The vignette therefore validates the
  model by spot-checking the closed-form equation against `rxSolve`
  output and by reproducing the typical-value trajectory + IIV envelope
  of Figure 2.
- **GWAS and post-hoc covariate findings not encoded.** The paper’s GWAS
  step uses individual-level theta1 and theta3 estimates (EBEs) as the
  phenotype for SNP association; the seven SNPs identified (rs347412,
  rs238349, rs559389, rs9366309, rs6763931, rs2304725, rs17161791) are
  downstream associations rather than covariates that enter the
  longitudinal model. They are not encoded in `covariateData` because
  they do not modify any structural parameter in the published fit.
- **Supplementary Tables E1 to E4 not on disk.** Supplements were not
  available during extraction (Phase 1 step 7 sidecar review). The cited
  supplementary tables (E1: AIC model comparison; E2: alternative theta3
  definition; E3: DGKH tissue expression; E4: NHGRI-catalog
  lung-function SNPs) describe model-selection rationale and downstream
  GWAS material rather than parameter values used in the final model;
  every final-model estimate this file consumes is in the main paper
  Table 2.
